    "# Signal Processing for Vibration Testing"
   ]
  },

   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 2,
   "metadata": {

   "source": [
    "%load_ext autoreload\n",
    "%autoreload 2\n",
    "%matplotlib inline\n",
    "\n",
    "import control as ctrl\n",
    "import matplotlib.pyplot as plt\n",
    "import vibrationtesting as vt\n",
    "import numpy as np\n",
    "import scipy as sp"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "Here we create a state space model to use in an \"experiment\". We will sample it at 1 kHz, and add a bit of noise. The input is on degree of freedom 1 (state 3), with two displacement sensors, one at each degree of freedom.  "
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 3,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "sample_freq = 1e3\n",
    "noise_power = 0.001 * sample_freq / 2\n",
    "A = sp.array([[0, 0, 1, 0],\\\n",
    "              [0, 0, 0, 1],\\\n",
    "              [-200, 100, -.2, .1],\\\n",
    "              [100, -200, .1, -.2]])\n",
    "B = sp.array([[0], [0], [1], [0]])\n",
    "C = sp.array([[35, 0, 0, 0], [0, 35, 0, 0]])\n",
    "D = sp.array([[0], [0]])\n",
    "sys = ctrl.ss(A, B, C, D)\n",
    "tin = sp.linspace(0, 204.8, num = 2048, endpoint = False)\n",
    "nr=.5   # Noise ratio. 0 is all noise on input"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "Now we simulate `num_exper` experiments. We also put some noise in the inputs and outputs after the simulation. Remember, we want to simulate measured inputs, to the noise on the input is the error in measuring that input. Likewise, noise is added to the output afterwards. If we had added noise to the input before the simulation, we would be simulating a known error in the input force. That's not nearly as hard to compensate for. "
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 9,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "if 'Yout' in vars(): del(Yout); del(Ucomb)  # Initialization line. \n",
    "num_exper = 25\n",
    "for i in sp.arange(num_exper): #was 2*50\n",
    "    u = np.random.normal(scale=sp.sqrt(noise_power), size=tin.shape)\n",
    "    t, yout, xout = ctrl.forced_response(sys, tin, u,rtol=1e-12,transpose=False)\n",
    "    if 'Yout' in locals():\n",
    "        Yout=np.dstack((Yout,yout+nr*np.random.normal(scale=.050*np.std(yout), size=yout.shape)))\n",
    "        Ucomb=np.dstack((Ucomb,u+(1-nr)*np.random.normal(scale=.05*np.std(u), size=u.shape)))\n",
    "    else:\n",
    "        # 5% half the noise on output as on input\n",
    "        Yout=yout+nr*np.random.normal(scale=.050*np.std(yout[0,:]), size=yout.shape)\n",
    "        # 10% noise signal on input\n",
    "        Ucomb=u+(1-nr)*np.random.normal(scale=.05*np.std(u), size=u.shape)#(1, len(tin))) "
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "There are 2048 time steps. "
   ]
  },

    "# Simultaneously plot all outputs resulting from the first excitation\n",
    "# This really makes no practical sense to do... but this is how you do it. \n",
    "# Note that we have to swap axes since we want to plot along the 2nd dimension (1-index)\n",
    "# but pyplot.plot plots along the 1st dimension (0-index). The notation used for data \n",
    "# makes more sense when plotting all outputs on the same dimension in the next cell. \n",

    "plt.ylabel('$y_n$, $n = 0, 1$')\n",

    "Due to the phenomenon called *leakage*, we often window the data. A common window used for such is the Hann window. You will often see if called hanning, but it was created by VonHann. There is a similar window, the *hamming* window by Hamming, which leads to the accidental mis-reference. \n",
    "\n",
    "The toolbox enables the user to directly obtain a window of the size necessary to window all data in all dimensions simply by using the raw data as an argument. Here one is plotted. They all will look the same, but the result is actually also a 2x2048x25 array. "
